The diagonal panels illustrate the posterior pdfs while the off-axis ones illustrate the correlation between the parameters. The vertical red lines and red crosses correspond to the best solution obtained from the down-hill simplex algorithm and used to initiate the 250 walkers. The vertical dashed lines locate the 16th and 84th percentiles.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=3&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201834573\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18.html#F3\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F4.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18-fig4_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F4.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 4.</span></a><p>Results of the MCMC sampling for the source position and lens galaxy centroid. The diagonal panels illustrate the posterior pdfs while the off-axis ones illustrate the correlation between the parameters. The vertical dashed lines locate the 16th and 84th percentiles.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=4&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201834573\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18.html#F4\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F5.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18-fig5_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F5.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 5.</span></a><p>GRAL 113100&#8722;441959 image configuration. The black dots locate the image positions, and their size mimics the associated flux, as reported in the <i>Gaia</i> DR2. The solid line represents the tangential critical line, the diamond-shaped dashed line represents the corresponding caustic line, and the dotted line defines the direction of the external shear. Finally, the color map shows how the surface mass density <i>&#954;</i> is distributed.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=5&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201834573\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18.html#F5\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F6.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18-fig6_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F6.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 6.</span></a><p>Model-predicted time delays scaled with <i>h</i>. The error bars combine the three sources of uncertainties described in the text. The gray shaded regions depict the contribution of the SPT to the error budget. The solid line corresponds to images C&#8722;D, the dashed line to C&#8722;A, and the dotted line to C&#8722;B. For the sake of clarity, we shifted upwards the time delays between images C&#8722;A (dashed line) by a three-day offset.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=6&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201834573\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18.html#F6\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F7.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/aa34573-18-fig7_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2019/08/aa34573-18/F7.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 7.</span></a><p>Example of histograms for &#916;<i>t</i><sub><i>ij</i></sub>&#8198;<i>h</i><sup>&#8722;1</sup> constructed for <i>z</i><sub>l</sub>&#8196;=&#8196;0.7 from the MCMC results. "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2019A&A...628A..17W", "Tables status": "Complete", "Inspection status": "Complete", "Paper Overview": {"abstract": "We report the spectroscopic confirmation and modeling of the quadruply imaged quasar GRAL 113100-441959, the first gravitational lens (GL) to be discovered from a machine learning technique that only relies on the relative positions and fluxes of the observed images without considering colour informations. Follow-up spectra obtained with Keck/LRIS reveal the lensing nature of this quadruply imaged quasar with redshift z<SUB>s</SUB> = 1.090 \u00b1 0.002, but show no evidence of the central lens galaxy. Using the image positions and G-band flux ratios provided by Gaia Data Release 2 as constraints, we modeled the system with a singular power-law elliptical mass distribution (SPEMD) plus external shear, to different levels of complexity. We show that relaxing the isothermal constraint of the SPEMD does not lead to statistically significant different results in terms of fitting the lensing data. We thus simplified the SPEMD to a singular isothermal ellipsoid to estimate the Einstein radius of the main lens galaxy \u03b8<SUB>E</SUB> = 0.\u2033851, the intensity and position angle of the external shear (\u03b3,\u03b8<SUB>\u03b3</SUB>) = (0.044, 11.\u00b05), and we predict the lensing galaxy position to be (\u03b8<SUB>gal,1</SUB>, \u03b8<SUB>gal,2</SUB>) = (-0.\u2033424, -0.\u2033744) with respect to image A. We provide time delay predictions for pairs of images, assuming a plausible range of lens redshift values z<SUB>l</SUB> between 0.5 and 0.9. Finally, we examine the impact on time delays of the so-called source position transformation, a family of degeneracies existing between different mass density profiles that reproduce most of the lensing observables equally well. We show that this effect contributes significantly to the time delay error budget and cannot be ignored during the modeling. This has implications for robust cosmography applications of lensed systems. GRAL 113100-441959 is the first in a series of seven new spectroscopically confirmed GLs discovered from Gaia Data Release 2.", "start_page": "A17", "authors": ["Wertz, O.", "Stern, D.", "Krone-Martins, A.", "Delchambre, L.", "Ducourant, C.", "Gr\u00e5e J\u00f8rgensen, U.", "Dominik, M.", "Burgdorf, M.", "Surdej, J.", "Mignard, F.", "Teixeira, R.", "Galluccio, L.", "Kl\u00fcter, J.", "Djorgovski, S.
